Section 1) Introduction
The Jepsen B-18-6190 well is a North lateral in the Middle Bakken. The well is located at NENW Section 19,
T161N R 90W in Burke Co. ND, USA. Surface coordinates are 335' FSL x 2000' FWL Section 19, T161N R90W. The
primary pay zone was defined as 7' to 14' in below the Middle Bakken Top. The objective was to steer the well within
the defined pay zone and within the legal requirements of the state. Directional and MWD services were performed by
Baker Hughes. Patrick Haley was the primary well site geologist assisted by Josef Peters, providing geo-steering and
mud logging from Columbine Logging, Inc.
1.1 Well Information
API #: 33-013-01805
Field: Northeast Foothills
Spud Date: 11/13/2014 TD Date: 11/30/2014
Surface Location: 335' FNL & 2000' FWL SEC 19, T161N, R90W, Burke County, North Dakota.
Intermediate Casing Point: 8045' MD, 7685.14' TVD: 363.83' FSL & 1993.94' FWL; SEC 18, T161N, R90W
Bottom Hole Location: 12,769' MD, 7,633.49' TVD: 5084.42' FSL & 2083.56' FWL; SEC 18, T164N, R90W
Surface Elevation: 2,025'

1.2 Well Summary
The Jepsen B-18-6190 is an extended reach single lateral production well in the Middle Bakken Formation in
Burke County, North Dakota. The well was drilled up-dip from south to north, crossing from Section 19 of T161N
R90W into Section 18 of T161N R90W, and followed an approximate azimuth of 0.37 degrees until reaching TD
coordinates of 12,769' MD, 7,633.49' TVD at 5084.42' FSL & 2083.56' FWL of Section 18, T161N, R90W. The target
pay zone was defined as approximately 14' feet thick and began 7' below the Middle Bakken Top. The initial Target
Top TVD was set as 7,672' TVD, Target Center at 7,679' TVD, and Target Base at 7,686' TVD based on the Middle
Bakken Top of 7664.97' TVD called at 7,906' MD while landing the curve.
The hot gamma ray facies (to approx. 150-160 API) seen around 14' below the Middle Bakken Top was
correlated with the Target centerline, a clean (low) gamma facies directly below the hot gamma ray facies (to approx.
30-50 API) was correlated with the lower 5 ½' of Target zone and another hot gamma ray facies (to approx. 120-140
API) was correlated with the target zone top. A "dead" gamma facies (82-95 API) was correlated with the target base
and lower out of zone portion of the formation. The overall apparent formation dip of this lateral was approximately
90.48°, with an average apparent formation dip of around 90.3°. At least two abrupt transitions between the top of
zone hot gamma and either the lower half of zone clean gamma or the "dead" gamma at the base of the zone were
encountered during the lateral. The abrupt transitions may possibly have been due to faulting or the thinning and/or
pinching out of the clean gamma facies.
7
8
Section 2) Services
2.1 Well site Geology Services (Columbine Logging, Inc.)
Geological consulting and mud logging started on 11/26/2014. Services provided included: gas monitoring,
morning and evening geological reports, 30' survey geological e-mail updates, sample collection, examination,
description and logging, sample pictures, and sample bagging and shipping of both curve and lateral samples,
production of the horizontal mud log including gas, ROP and gamma curves, geo-steering, and a final End Of Well
report.
2.1.1 Gas Detection
Gas was logged using a Bloodhound total gas/chromatograph system. The gas detection system uses an
infra-red detector to measure total gas and the chromatograph separates and measures gases C1, C2, C3, iC4 and
nC4. Gas was recorded in units where 1 unit equals 100 ppm. The gas detection system measured gases: C1, C2,
C3, IC4, NC4, H2S, O2 and CO2.
The Bloodhound Gas Detection and Chromatograph system use digital signal processing techniques and
non-dispersive infrared and chemical sensors for gas detection. The system uses a proprietary chromatograph, which
has the capability to detect from 0 to 10,000 gas units. This translates as 0 to 100% typical naturally-occurring
hydrocarbon gas mixtures. Calibration is performed using National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST)
traceable calibration gases. Lab calibration points include 0%, 2.5%, and 100% pure methane. Complete immunity to
saturation or damage in the presence of high concentrations of both light and heavy hydrocarbon gases precludes the
necessity of constant re-calibration or zero referencing. This allows the Bloodhound to react to hydrocarbon based
gases from zero to 100% in concentration without dilution.
Lag time was approximated from a calculation of annular velocity based on: pump output, open-hole
diameter, cased hole diameter, collar diameter, drill pipe diameter and bottom hole assembly. Connection gases were
monitored to confirm lag time calculations and thereby adjust lag time as needed.
2.1.2 Mud Logging
Mud Logging services were provided for the Jepsen B-18-6190 from the Intermediate casing point at 8,045'
MD through the lateral section of the well to TD at 12,769' MD. A Horizontal Mud Log was compiled and created
during the drilling of the Jepsen B18-6190 well.
8
9
2.1.3 Geosteering
The primary offset GR vs TVD log for the landing correlation was the Jepsen 21-19HB. Based on formation
isopach maps, the Middle Bakken was estimated to be 42' feet thick at landing, thinning to around 36' near proposed
TD. Gamma patterns were compared with the offset log and a GR vs. TVD plot was created with gamma data
recorded while landing the curve in order to correlate the formation gamma encountered in the lateral with the target
zone GR data. Within the Middle Bakken the primary objective was to stay in the middle of the 14' target zone near
the hot gamma marker without going above the hot gamma at the top of zone or below into the dead gamma at the
zone base.
Steering in the lateral was accomplished by using dips ranging from 89.62° to 91.86° by correlation of
relevant gamma markers: The hot gamma ray marker (150-160 API) correlated to the Target centerline, the lower
zone clean gamma facies directly below the hot gamma ray facies (30-50 API), the hot gamma ray facies (120-140
API) at the target zone top, and the dead gamma facies (82-95 API) encountered at and below the target base.
Additionally, sample lithology, total gas, and ROP data attained from the Pason EDR System were used to determine
our position within the formation.
9
10
Section 3) Geology
3.1 Samples
Sample analysis began at 8070' MD in the Middle Bakken Formation. See Horizontal logs for complete
lithology descriptions and pictures.
3.1.1 Sample Examination
Samples were collected every 30 Ft. from just outside the Intermediate casing point at 8,070' MD to 12,769'
MD' while drilling the lateral. Descriptions included: mineralogy, color, firmness, argillaceous content, structure,
texture, allochems, porosity, oil stain, and hydrocarbon fluorescence. Carbonate identification and percentages were
determined using 10% dilute HCl, and alizarin red. Hydrocarbon fluorescence was determined using a fluoroscope
with a UV lamp.
Descriptions of typical samples from formation facies correlated with GR while drilling the lateral include:
Target Zone Center Samples (Hot GR 150-160 API)
10770'-10830': 50% SHALY SLITSTONE: light-very dark gray, white-cream, mottled, firm, sub blocky-platy,
argillaceous, imbedded pyrite, loose pyrite nodules, moderately calcareous cement, 30% LIMESTONE: white, very
light gray, sub blocky, firm, microcrystalline, packstone; 20% SANDSTONE: light gray - light tan, translucent, poorly
consolidated, very fine grained, well rounded, moderately sorted, abundant loose quartz grains; Oil Show:
scattered yellow mineral florescence, moderately fast streaming bright white cut, trace brown stain.
Target Zone Bottom Half Samples (Clean GR 30-50 API)
10530'-10590': 75% LIMESTONE: white, very light gray, sub blocky, firm, microcrystalline, oolitic, packstone. 20%
SANDSTONE: light gray - light tan, translucent, poorly-moderately consolidated, very fine grained, well rounded,
moderately sorted, trace loose quartz grains; 5% SILTSTONE: white-cream, light-very dark gray, mottled, firm, sub
blocky-platy, dolomitic cement. Oil Show: trace yellow mineral florescence, slow diffuse blue-white cut, trace green
stain.
Target Zone Base Samples (Dead GR 82-95 API)
8910'-8970': 85% SILTSTONE: white-cream, light-very dark gray, mottled, firm,
sub blocky-sub angular, very fine grained, calcareous cement, trace shaly; 10% SANDSTONE; clear, tan,
translucent-transparent, unconsolidated, well rounded, well sorted, loose quartz grains; 5% LIMESTONE:
white, very light gray, sub blocky, firm, microcrystalline, oolitic, packstone. Oil Show: trace
yellow/white mineral florescence, trace slow streaming white cut, no stain.

3.3 Lateral Breakdown
The well has a total producing lateral length of 4,699' with the following in-zone statistics:
Middle Bakken: 4699' (100%)
Drilling Target Breakdown as follows:
Above Drilling Target Footage =
64' (1.36%)
Inside Drilling Target Footage =
2,898' (61.68%)
Below Drilling target Footage =
1,737' (36.96%)
In-zone percentages are estimated based on the dead gamma occurring at the base of the target zone only.
In-zone percentages may increase significantly through correlation with dead gamma occurring within the bottom 1'-
1.5'of the target zone. Formation dip cannot be accurately calculated or estimated while the well bore is in the dead
gamma.
3.4 Formation Dip
The overall apparent formation dip of this lateral was approximately 90.48°, with an average apparent
formation dip of around 90.3°. At least two abrupt facies transitions were encountered during the lateral; one at
around 9,100' MD between the top center zone hot gamma and the "dead" gamma at the base of the zone. The next
abrupt facies transition was encountered around 11,810' MD between the top of zone hot gamma and the lower half
of zone clean gamma facies. The abrupt transitions may have been due to either faulting or the thinning or pinching
out of the clean gamma facies. Thus, at least one, and possibly two, faults were encountered during the drilling of the
lateral portion of the well. These transitions dropped the wellbore in section at each occurrence, and have the effect of
increasing overall dip above average formation dip.
11
12
Section 4) Well History
4.1 Overall Lateral Section
The curve was landed at the base of the target zone in the Middle Bakken at 8,066' MD (7,679' TVD). The
curve was landed 7' high to the prognosed target horizon. As we drilled out of intermediate casing, we encountered
an average apparent dip of 89.71° until around 8,600' MD, where the formation dip steepened to an apparent dip of
90.11° until around 9,000' MD (See Fig 4.1 Overall Lateral Section View of the Horizontal, following page).
At around 9,000' MD to 9,100' MD, an abrupt transition from the top half of zone GR and lithology to the dead gamma
at the base of the zone occurred. No GR markers typically encountered (i.e. center hot GR and clean lower zone GR
facies) from the top of the zone down in section to the base of zone were encountered in this section of the lateral.
This transition had the effect of dropping the wellbore in section some 7' to 8'. Dip then steepened again to an
apparent dip of 90.3° from 9,000' MD to around 10,815'MD. At 10,815'MD, very hot gamma believed to be the target
center GR marker was encountered, resulting in a dip increase from 90.3° to around 91.86° for the next 200' of lateral.
At around 11,020' MD, the well bore encountered the dead gamma at the base of the zone again; here, the
steepening of apparent dip to 91.86° may have been caused by the pinching out of the clean gamma facies. The
wellbore then climbed through section having an apparent formation dip of 90.2°-90.3° until reaching the top of zone
Hot GR marker at approximately 11,780' MD. By 11,812' MD the wellbore was again in the clean GR marker at the
lower half of the target zone; here, it is highly likely the wellbore crossed a fault with approximately 7'-8' of throw,
dropping the wellbore at least 7' in section. The wellbore then came down through the clean GR facies to the base
zone dead gamma at 12,030' MD then back up to the clean facies at around 12,590' MD through an average
apparent formation dip of 90.51° until reaching TD of the well.
The lateral was drilled to TD at 12,769' MD, 7,633.49' TVD at 5084.42' FSL & 2083.56' FWL of Section 18,
T161N, R90W; Burke County, North Dakota USA.
Gas values were generally low (< 400u) in the bottom of the zone and significantly higher (1000u-2000u) at
the zone center and top.

Section 6) Summary and Conclusion
The Jepsen B-18-6190 well is a North lateral in the Middle Bakken. The well is located at NENW Section 19,
T161N R 90W in Burke Co. ND, USA. Surface coordinates are 335' FSL x 2000' FWL Section 19, T161N R90W. The
primary pay zone was defined as 7' to 14' in below the Middle Bakken Top. This pay zone was picked for its
production potential and quality of reservoir rock. The objective was to steer the well within the defined pay zone and
within the legal requirements of the state.
The anticipated dip of the formation was between 90.3 - 90.7°, based on a subsurface structure map provided
by Cornerstone Natural Resources, LLC. The primary offset GR-TVD log was the Jepsen 21-19HB. The well was
drilled up-dip from south to north, crossing from Section 19 of T161N R90W into Section 18 of T161N R90W, and
followed an approximate azimuth of 0.37 degrees until reaching TD coordinates of 12,769' MD, 7,633.49' TVD at
5084.42' FSL & 2083.56' FWL of Section 18, T161N, R90W.
The overall apparent formation dip of this lateral was approximately 90.48°, with an average apparent
formation dip of around 90.3°. At least two abrupt facies transitions were encountered during the lateral; one at
around 9,100' MD and one encountered around 11,810' MD. The abrupt transitions were due to either faulting or the
thinning or pinching out of the clean gamma facies. At least one (possibly two) fault was encountered during the
drilling of the lateral portion of the well. These transitions/fault(s) dropped the wellbore in section and have the effect
of increasing overall dip above average formation dip.
The objective while drilling the lateral was to keep the wellbore inside the 14' widow of our target zone. Gas
readings were highest in the center of our zone and lowest near and past the base of our zone. The in-zone
percentage of 61.68% (2,898') was estimated based on the dead gamma occurring at the base of the target zone
only. In-zone percentages may increase significantly through correlation with dead gamma occurring within the bottom
1'-1.5'of the target zone. Formation apparent dip could not be accurately estimated while the well bore was in the
dead gamma.
Currently the well is awaiting completion.

Dear SHANNON:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 22892, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The approval is
granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than the 200' setback from
the north & south boundaries and 1220' setback (per Commission policy) from the east & west boundaries within the 1280
acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 7 & 18 T161N-R90W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for filter sock
disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must remain on-site during
clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are conducted. In cases where a spacing unit
is accessed from an off-site drill pad, an affidavit must be provided affirming that the surface owner of the multi-
well pad agrees to accept burial on their property of the cuttings generated from drilling the well(s) into an offsite
spacing/drilling unit. CORNERSTONE NAT RES LLC must contact NDIC Field Inspector Jim Potts at 701-
720-3023 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well drilling and
completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will prevent pollution of
the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits are prohibited. All pits shall be
inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use. Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized
in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC. The
proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing point is: 535'N.
Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the well head is: 10711'N.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the approved
drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to commence before the 3rd
business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may be waived by the Director.
Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information necessary to evaluate the extenuating
circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other information that would allow the Director to
conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested that
notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas
Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00
p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours or on the weekend.

September 2, 2014
Page 2
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor shall file a
certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys must be submitted as
one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may require the directional survey to be
filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the operation of the director's office in a timely manner.
Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve (or when
sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12 hours, and tail
cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi before drilling the plug or
initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

Jepsen B and Jepsen 21-19 locations.pdf
Good afternoon Alice,
Attached is a google earth map showing the existing Jepson 21-19 location with the pumping unit,
tanks, etc. and the new Jepsen B well spotted to the north. I would like to put the production
facilities on the Jepsen 21-19 to reduce the environmental impact to the new location and allow us
to reclaim more of it after we are finished completing the well. I would put the tanks for the Jepsen
B on the south side of the existing tanks on the Jepsen 21-19 pad, the treater next to the existing
treater and the flare by the existing flare for the 21-19. We would then run our production line
from the Jepsen B wellhead south to the Jepsen 21-19 pad and tie in at the treater.
Let me know if this works for you. Feel free to call my cell anytime.
Thanks,
